  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_db803b4e-68f3-4e51-8aa7-6cd306524ce9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

  <span id="freeText5020508435723447308" style="display:none">A compelling and perceptive tale of intimacy, memory and relationships from the No.1 bestselling author.<br /><br />How can you know someone you’ve never met?<br /><br />Joyce Conway remembers things she shouldn't. She knows about tiny cobbled streets in Paris, which she has never visited. And every night she dreams about an unknown little girl with blonde hair.<br /><br />Justin Hitchcock is divorced, lonely and restless. He arrives in Dublin to give a lecture on art and meets an attractive doctor, who persuades him to donate blood. It's the first thing to come straight from his heart in a long time.<br /><br />When Joyce leaves hospital after a terrible accident, with her life and her marriage in pieces, she moves back in with her elderly father. All the while, a strong sense of déjà vu is overwhelming her and she can't figure out why …</span>

<div id="review_231852269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/231852269" />
    <a title="Mansi Sharma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5503458-mansi-sharma"><img alt="Mansi Sharma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307877351p2/5503458.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231852269?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mansi Sharma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mansi Sharma" href="/user/show/5503458-mansi-sharma">Mansi Sharma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5503458-mansi-sharma?shelf=books-i-will-keep-coming-back-to">books-i-will-keep-coming-back-to</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5503458-mansi-sharma?shelf=cecelia-ahern">cecelia-ahern</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231852269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1716018467052877161"><i>"Sometimes we need all the glue we can get, just to hold ourselves together."</i> This is one book that I just didn't want to have an end. It taught me so much. Specially the things that I knew but couldn't quite come one to. <b>Thanks for the Memories</b> has two parallel stories looking for one common destination. An Irish woman Joyce has just had a tsunami of troubled times in her life. She's going through the loss of her unborn child, a failed marriage and has to face all those sorry faces that she cou</span>
  <span id="freeText1716018467052877161" style="display:none"><i>"Sometimes we need all the glue we can get, just to hold ourselves together."</i> This is one book that I just didn't want to have an end. It taught me so much. Specially the things that I knew but couldn't quite come one to. <b>Thanks for the Memories</b> has two parallel stories looking for one common destination. An Irish woman Joyce has just had a tsunami of troubled times in her life. She's going through the loss of her unborn child, a failed marriage and has to face all those sorry faces that she could clearly do without. She has her 75 year old father with her (the best best BEST character in the book who'd make you laugh your hearts out), and her two best friends, indeed. An American man Justin, who has moved across the country just to be close to his daughter Bea, is recovering from his divorce. An art and architecture freak, he comes to Dublin as a guest lecturer and has to donate his blood just to get in the good books of this gorgeous doctor Sarah. This blood saves Joyce's life when she has the miscarriage. After the blood transfusion, Joyce learns Latin and Italian overnight; apart from the great, great knowledge about the Renaissance Paintings and architecture. The rest is for you to find out! :P<br />It is an amazing, amazing story which would make you laugh and smile through the tears. This fiction, ironically, will help you a great deal in going through the reality and not to forget, a better understanding of life and death and everything in between!<br /><br />Happy Reading! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1716018467052877161" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12928294529870894279"><i>How is it possible to know someone you've never met?<br/><br/>With her marriage already in pieces, Joyce Conway nearly lost everything else. But she survived the terrible accident - and now, inexplicably, she can remember faces she has never seen, cobblestone Parisian streets she's never visited.</i><br/><br/>Thanks For The Memories is like a bubble gum, it stretches until it bursts. And unfortunately my patience stretched and burst with it and then I wasn't interested in what was to happen next, not at all. I indeed w</span>
  <span id="freeText12928294529870894279" style="display:none"><i>How is it possible to know someone you've never met?<br /><br />With her marriage already in pieces, Joyce Conway nearly lost everything else. But she survived the terrible accident - and now, inexplicably, she can remember faces she has never seen, cobblestone Parisian streets she's never visited.</i><br /><br />Thanks For The Memories is like a bubble gum, it stretches until it bursts. And unfortunately my patience stretched and burst with it and then I wasn't interested in what was to happen next, not at all. I indeed wouldn't mind if Joyce went nuts and killed everyone around her, well, perhaps I would be even glad because it would be more interesting than waiting for her encounter with Justin all the time.<br /><br />And I didn't like Justin, he was sooo selfish and such a pig to Sarah and then there is that odd blood transfusion.. Occasional fits of laughter and my resolve not to abandon yet another book were the only things that made me finish it, neverthless I skimmed a lot and the ending wasn't worth the effort. I was waiting for one scene, expecting it to be great and that scene came only at the very last pages and left me mad. Was I waiting for <b>that</b> all the time?!</span>

<div id="review_90935954" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90935954" />
    <a title="Meghan Cooper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3320580-meghan-cooper"><img alt="Meghan Cooper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268173833p2/3320580.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90935954?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meghan Cooper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meghan Cooper" href="/user/show/3320580-meghan-cooper">Meghan Cooper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007233694" href="/book/show/3177191-thanks-for-the-memories">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Meghan by: </span>
      Friend
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3320580-meghan-cooper?shelf=holiday-books">holiday-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90935954" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2399305138393692063">I finished Thanks For The Memories last night at about 10.30. I read a full 300 hundred pages in the evening. Maybe slightly obsessive, but It was a rather addictive story! It’s really hard to judge this book by its cover, it is so pretty and the colours are just lovely!<br/>Thanks For The Memories by Cecelia Ahern is her fifth book to be published and is definitely my favourite so far.<br/><br/> It follows Joyce as she comes to term with the loss of her unborn baby due to an accident falling down the stairs. </span>
  <span id="freeText2399305138393692063" style="display:none">I finished Thanks For The Memories last night at about 10.30. I read a full 300 hundred pages in the evening. Maybe slightly obsessive, but It was a rather addictive story! It’s really hard to judge this book by its cover, it is so pretty and the colours are just lovely!<br />Thanks For The Memories by Cecelia Ahern is her fifth book to be published and is definitely my favourite so far.<br /><br /> It follows Joyce as she comes to term with the loss of her unborn baby due to an accident falling down the stairs. She feels this strange connection though with a random man she meets in a hairdressers. She is also remembering some one elses memories. She dreams of a little girl with blonde hair and of places she’s never been. She miraculously learns italian overnight. She follows her heart and finds out what’s behind all of these strange happenings.<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book because I loved the whole idea and concept that Ahern came up with. Also I enjoyed the romance between them even though they only speak two or three times in the book. I can imagine them marrying and everything, Ahern gave you enough just to let you imagine what happens next. My favourite part of this books concoction of good points was the humor. With Cecelia Ahern’s other books I didn’t laugh at all, it was more crying related, with Thanks for the Memories I laughed so much. I loved the whole excursion to London with her father. Her crazy, funny and sweet father is what made this novel colourful for me. He added the extra dimension.<br /><br />On the other hand it would have been nicer if the book had of had more time of the two main characters together. It felt almost unfinished. There were lots of circles in the plot, but this is quite like Ahern’s style of writing and it has been apparent in her other books. I was quite confused at the beginning as to what had happened to Joyce, I thought she had been in a car accident and I think that it would have worked without her having to lose her baby. I didn’t really understand how she would need a blood transfusion from that…. Also the beginning prologue didn’t really grab my attention. <br /><br />Overall this novel was full of funny characters, hilarious jokes, romantic sections and the novel was fast-moving. To make it better Ahern needs to add more bulk to her storylines. It was an excellent idea though.<br /><br />My Favourite Part: When Joyce and her father visit the antique roadshow and steal a bin and get on television for it! Never laughed so much. Also when they go on the viking bus!<br /><br />Saddest Part: When she moves in with her father and sees the blood stain on the carpet from when she fell and lost her baby… <br /><br />Cutest Part: When Justin chases after Joyce’s Viking Bus. Ah and then he calls out her name even though he doesn’t know it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2399305138393692063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_60752798" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60752798" />
    <a title="Ailsa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/135952-ailsa"><img alt="Ailsa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1427767025p2/135952.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60752798?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ailsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ailsa" href="/user/show/135952-ailsa">Ailsa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/135952-ailsa?shelf=women-writers">women-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/135952-ailsa?shelf=light-read">light-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/135952-ailsa?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer60752798&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60752798" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16549274531240350038">I have read a few of Cecelia Ahern's novels now (although not her most famous, P.S I love You) and to be perfectly honest, I'm not sure what the hype is about. Maybe in my old age I'm just too cynical for Ahern's brand of *~magical~* romances.<br/><br/>Its not even solely that the premise (girl and boy gain long distance connection through blood transfusion) requires a massive suspension of disbelief. If there was any sort of real romantic pay-off I could accept quite a lot from a writer. But this story l</span>
  <span id="freeText16549274531240350038" style="display:none">I have read a few of Cecelia Ahern's novels now (although not her most famous, P.S I love You) and to be perfectly honest, I'm not sure what the hype is about. Maybe in my old age I'm just too cynical for Ahern's brand of *~magical~* romances.<br /><br />Its not even solely that the premise (girl and boy gain long distance connection through blood transfusion) requires a massive suspension of disbelief. If there was any sort of real romantic pay-off I could accept quite a lot from a writer. But this story left me cold, mostly because I don't actually find it that romantic that you discover you're "perfect" for this guy once you've basically had your entire personality excised by his blood. No joke, Joyce, the character in this novel goes from being a fun loving, vegetarian, estate agent to an authority of architechture (leading to her being unable to perform her job), a speaker of several languages, a bit of a kill joy and a rabid meat eater. And then she can meet the man of "her" dreams (actually the man of the memories she's dreaming that have somehow been transmitted to her). I'm sorry, but what about being completely obliterated as a person ranks as romantic?<br /><br />Even more than my problems with this point of the plot is the fact that, in an attempt to extend the initial mystery of the novel's set up, we spend almost the entire book getting to the "good" bits of any romance - and its not even as if the novel had me in suspense. About 20 pages in it became obvious what had happened, so I was just wading through wondering when I was going to reach the romantic meeting/ realisation of these characters.<br /><br />In an attempt to not be completely negative, I will say that there were some good secondary characters in this novel (Joyce's dad in particular) and it wasn't an absolute chore to read. Eseentially it was a mindlessly sort-of enjoyable and entirely forgettable read. And that's the closest to an endorsement you're going to get from me. Unfortunately, I require a little bit more, even if it is "only" chick lit.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16549274531240350038" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575576897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1723842034786909033"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2410506.Thanks_for_the_Memories' title='Thanks for the Memories by Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thanks for the Memories</a> is a standalone, women's fiction novel written by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern' title='Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cecelia Ahern</a>. This book has a bit of magical realism added to it that gave it a pretty unique storyline. Imagine having a blood transfusion and suddenly being linked to the donor and vice versa. Pretty unreal, huh? Overall, I thought <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2410506.Thanks_for_the_Memories' title='Thanks for the Memories by Cecelia Ahern' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thanks for the Memories</a> was fun, sweet, and creative. But...Ms. Ahern took the slow lane on the highway just to go to the corner store in my opinion. This would have been the perfect plot for</span>
  <span id="freeText1723842034786909033" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2410506.Thanks_for_the_Memories" title="Thanks for the Memories by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Thanks for the Memories</a> is a standalone, women's fiction novel written by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern" title="Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Cecelia Ahern</a>. This book has a bit of magical realism added to it that gave it a pretty unique storyline. Imagine having a blood transfusion and suddenly being linked to the donor and vice versa. Pretty unreal, huh? Overall, I thought <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2410506.Thanks_for_the_Memories" title="Thanks for the Memories by Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Thanks for the Memories</a> was fun, sweet, and creative. But...Ms. Ahern took the slow lane on the highway just to go to the corner store in my opinion. This would have been the perfect plot for a short story versus a full-length novel. It's slow-going and long and I felt it for sure. I won't be reading this for a second time but it was an OK read overall. I had to add a star to my initial 2-star rating because you know it's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7116.Cecelia_Ahern" title="Cecelia Ahern" rel="nofollow noopener">Cecelia Ahern</a> ♥<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>“We all get lost once in a while, sometimes by choice, sometimes due to forces beyond our control. When we learn what it is our soul needs to learn, the path presents itself. Sometimes we see the way out but wander further and deeper despite ourselves; the fear, the anger or the sadness preventing us returning. Sometimes we prefer to be lost and wandering, sometimes it's easier. Sometimes we find our own way out. But regardless, always, we are found.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1723842034786909033" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer21838324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7201049278439420163">What a wonderful book!!!! This book was one of those rare books that grabbed me from the first chapter, one that you can't put down, you just have to keep reading to find out what is going to happen to the characters and you read as fast as you possibly can.<br/>This was such a beautifully told story from the first page to the last. I loved the diversity of the characters, the pain, the relationships, I laughed until I nearly cried and then I cried when I felt their pain.<br/>The story is set mainly in Ir</span>
  <span id="freeText7201049278439420163" style="display:none">What a wonderful book!!!! This book was one of those rare books that grabbed me from the first chapter, one that you can't put down, you just have to keep reading to find out what is going to happen to the characters and you read as fast as you possibly can.<br />This was such a beautifully told story from the first page to the last. I loved the diversity of the characters, the pain, the relationships, I laughed until I nearly cried and then I cried when I felt their pain.<br />The story is set mainly in Ireland and in a clever way tells you about a lot of the local architecture. It is about 2 people whose lives cross in a most unusual way and their, at times hilarious interactions with their own families and friends. There is a scene in a hotel room between Joyce and her Dad when they laugh hysterically and just can't stop, then her elderly father laughs so hard he farts (her word not mine) and then has a little 'accident'. This scene was so funny I had tears rolling down my face. It also had a touch of fairytale magic in it, yet was more a story about family relationships than romance.<br />So thank you to Cecelia Ahern for a very entertaining book, I will definitely read more of your books now!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7201049278439420163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_113468276" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113468276" />
    <a title="FreshGrads .Sg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3908133-freshgrads-sg"><img alt="FreshGrads .Sg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1283141230p2/3908133.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113468276?book_show_action=true">Jul 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="FreshGrads .Sg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="FreshGrads .Sg" href="/user/show/3908133-freshgrads-sg">FreshGrads .Sg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113468276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17328133154294867311">Thanks for the Memories is the latest book by Cecelia Ahern, acclaimed author of bestseller PS I Love You as well as the youngest daughter of former Irish Prime Minister Bertie Ahern. The 28-year-old seems to have all going well for her: Her third novel, If You Could See Me Now, will be the second novel adaptation hitting the screens soon while her fourth novel, A Place Called Here, is to be made into a US TV series.<br/><br/>After a devastating miscarriage which also spells the last of her fast falling a</span>
  <span id="freeText17328133154294867311" style="display:none">Thanks for the Memories is the latest book by Cecelia Ahern, acclaimed author of bestseller PS I Love You as well as the youngest daughter of former Irish Prime Minister Bertie Ahern. The 28-year-old seems to have all going well for her: Her third novel, If You Could See Me Now, will be the second novel adaptation hitting the screens soon while her fourth novel, A Place Called Here, is to be made into a US TV series.<br /><br />After a devastating miscarriage which also spells the last of her fast falling apart marriage, Joyce Conway moves in with her muddled and eccentric father. She begins recalling memories that do not belong to her. Instead, they belong to Justin Hitchcock, a divorced architecture guest lecturer in Dublin.<br /><br />Despite reading several rave reviews of Thanks for the Memories and of the author herself, I was unable to apprehend the book's success. Barely reading up to a third of the book, it became so obvious what happened that it left me wondering when I would reach the romantic climax. I must say, I was kept waiting for a pretty long time. First I had to suspend all disbelief of the premise that two individuals might be connected through a blood transfusion. Second, after much waiting, there was hardly much of a romantic climax per say. The two instantly deemed each other perfect upon finding out the source of their connection. Third, the book delivers far less than expected – characters show much promise with fun-loving, vegetarian Joyce and a geeky-cute architecture lecturer of a love interest. Interestingly, the supporting cast, Joyce's father, proves much more entertaining to read instead.<br /><br />That said, it was characters like this that kept me through the book. Otherwise, Thanks for the Memories was hardly a chick lit read and only worth an attempt by Ahern's avid fans.<br /><br />For more book reviews, visit <a href="http://www.freshgrads.sg/index.php/articles/lifestyle/read.html" rel="nofollow noopener"> FreshGrads Reads</a>. We also do reviews on food, movies and more in Singapore. Check us out <a href="www.FreshGrads.Sg" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17328133154294867311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Sandra Grauschopf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2786009-sandra-grauschopf"><img alt="Sandra Grauschopf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1266315060p2/2786009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154824212?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandra Grauschopf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandra Grauschopf" href="/user/show/2786009-sandra-grauschopf">Sandra Grauschopf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780007233694" href="/book/show/3177191-thanks-for-the-memories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154824212" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer802856064400824550">I picked up this book because of the blurb on the back that said, "Cecelia Ahern is queen of the modern fairytale." I love fairytales, and I thought that a chick lit book with a fairytale feel would be awesome.<br/><br/>But it seems that whoever wrote that blurb has never actually read a fairytale, only knows that they have something to do with magic. Or something. And this book does have one incredibly unlikely magical element, which is already hard to buy into. <br/><br/>So you know that the hero and the heroine </span>
  <span id="freeText802856064400824550" style="display:none">I picked up this book because of the blurb on the back that said, "Cecelia Ahern is queen of the modern fairytale." I love fairytales, and I thought that a chick lit book with a fairytale feel would be awesome.<br /><br />But it seems that whoever wrote that blurb has never actually read a fairytale, only knows that they have something to do with magic. Or something. And this book does have one incredibly unlikely magical element, which is already hard to buy into. <br /><br />So you know that the hero and the heroine are fated to be together from the very beginning. Unfortunately, they're both too childish, immature, and downright stupid to be able to manage it. The book would be about 50 pages long, if either character had a grain of sense to them. Since they don't, they manage to drag on the tale for 489 pages, by the end of which, I was hoping more for some kind of crippling accident to put them out of my misery than the promised "happy ending." <br /><br />But lo, there was no "rocks fall, everyone dies" moment, and everyone is happy by the end. Lalalala.<br /><br />Whatever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="802856064400824550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1733595682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1733595682" />
    <a title="Shaikha Alahmad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/55334362-shaikha-alahmad"><img alt="Shaikha Alahmad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583758717p2/55334362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1733595682?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shaikha Alahmad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shaikha Alahmad" href="/user/show/55334362-shaikha-alahmad">Shaikha Alahmad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/19100438-thanks-for-the-memories">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1733595682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3386647533594939821"><b>
  <i>”He told me that story way back when I sucked my thumb and when he was as big as an oak tree. When mum’s yawns sounded like songs. When we were all together. When I had no idea there would ever come a time when we wouldn’t be. When we used to have chats in the garden, under the weeping willow. Where I always used to hide and where he always found me. When nothing was impossible and when the three of us, together forever, was a given.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><b>3.5/5</b><br/><br/>The narrative follows two very different people as th</span>
  <span id="freeText3386647533594939821" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”He told me that story way back when I sucked my thumb and when he was as big as an oak tree. When mum’s yawns sounded like songs. When we were all together. When I had no idea there would ever come a time when we wouldn’t be. When we used to have chats in the garden, under the weeping willow. Where I always used to hide and where he always found me. When nothing was impossible and when the three of us, together forever, was a given.”</i>
</b><br /><br /><b>3.5/5</b><br /><br />The narrative follows two very different people as their lives begin to entwine. Justin is visiting Dublin to give a lecture on art and is persuaded to give blood. Joyce has just awoken after a terrible accident which has caused her to lose her baby and, by the looks of it, her marriage too. After the accident she has a blood transfusion to save her life and suddenly remembers things that have never happened to her, and information she didn't know before. The pair have never met and yet are magically drawn to one another, due to Justin's blood saving Joyce's life.<br /><br />Both Joyce and Justin have become despondent with their lives; Joyce moves in with her father after the accident and her marriage falls apart. Justin is divorced and spends most of his time traveling around giving lectures to students that he feels really aren't that interested. Their paths cross several times throughout the story, and each time they meet they become ever closer.<br /><br />I cried and I laughed more than I thought I would. The narrative is somewhat predictable and the story got slow and boring at times, but <i>Thanks for the Memories</i> is still a compelling read and makes for a delightful, if somewhat unbelievable, love story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3386647533594939821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1974165234" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Susan in Perthshire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44004632-susan-in-perthshire"><img alt="Susan in Perthshire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595083509p2/44004632.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1974165234?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susan in Perthshire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susan in Perthshire" href="/user/show/44004632-susan-in-perthshire">Susan in Perthshire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11746144-thanks-for-the-memories">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44004632-susan-in-perthshire?shelf=romantic-fiction">romantic-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1974165234" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer6218285599626828957">I normally enjoy Cecelia Ahern's books. Firstly, she writes with elegance, humour and skill; and her books draw you in to a world that is often strange and whimsical, but nonetheless very real and believable. I liked the sound of this one - the little teasers piqued my interest and I thought 'this sounds good'. It started well, good character development and scene setting so that I was drawn in very quickly. Then ... I just lost interest or perhaps concern about the characters. I just did not ca</span>
  <span id="freeText6218285599626828957" style="display:none">I normally enjoy Cecelia Ahern's books. Firstly, she writes with elegance, humour and skill; and her books draw you in to a world that is often strange and whimsical, but nonetheless very real and believable. I liked the sound of this one - the little teasers piqued my interest and I thought 'this sounds good'. It started well, good character development and scene setting so that I was drawn in very quickly. Then ... I just lost interest or perhaps concern about the characters. I just did not care what happened to them. It was okay - a great beach read - but I was disappointed. So much so, that I abandoned it half way through and returned to it many weeks later! I never do that with books so I am mystified. It might just be me so I am reluctant to condemn it but I just could not get excited. </span>

<div id="review_53823434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53823434" />
    <a title="Marty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/126461-marty"><img alt="Marty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1260155706p2/126461.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53823434?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marty" href="/user/show/126461-marty">Marty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126461-marty?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/126461-marty?shelf=harpercollins">harpercollins</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53823434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6953296951437209784">Honestly, I wasn't a huge fan of this book. It took me a while to figure out what the problem was, because it's not that Ahern can't write. The prologue is beautifully written and sets up an intriguing mystery. Who is this woman? How pregnant is she? Has she lost the baby? How did she fall down the stairs? Who was on the phone? <br/><br/>I couldn't wait to get into the book and find out what happened. And then - I just didn't believe it. And I'm not even talking about the plot, as implausible as it is. (B</span>
  <span id="freeText6953296951437209784" style="display:none">Honestly, I wasn't a huge fan of this book. It took me a while to figure out what the problem was, because it's not that Ahern can't write. The prologue is beautifully written and sets up an intriguing mystery. Who is this woman? How pregnant is she? Has she lost the baby? How did she fall down the stairs? Who was on the phone? <br /><br />I couldn't wait to get into the book and find out what happened. And then - I just didn't believe it. And I'm not even talking about the plot, as implausible as it is. (Boy donates blood, girl gets boy's blood after falling down the stairs, girls suddenly has all of the dude's memories.) The problem was that I didn't believe the characters, at all. They didn't seem like real people, they seemed like devices to churn the plot. <br /><br />I feel the need to give examples of what I mean, though they probably will seem petty. Joyce's dad is described as having planned his entire life out, yet when they're in London doesn't know how to pack a suitcase and makes a disaster of it. It seems like anyone who is all about organization should be able to fold his clothes and put them in a bag. Joyce, on the other hand, is described as just rushing into things in life without thinking them through - yet she's spent the past ten years redecorating her house in a loveless marriage. Really? So, she flies by the seat of her pants, but no affairs or other craziness outside of choosing drapes in all those years of boredom? Ooooooo-kay.<br /><br />Other stupid things that annoyed me: Justin, the boy blood donor, makes a slightly cheeky remark at an elderly lady in the dentist waiting room. Her response is to throw a magazine at his head. Really? That's just not really something people do, and Justin appears unsurprised and just keeps walking away. Then, Joyce again. She miscarries in the middle of her second trimester, and in one scene there is very detailed description of her pulling on her jeans. So ... she's already back in pre-pregnancy jeans? And if so, she doesn't feel a pang or anything about that during the FIVE PAGES she's busy pulling them on? <br /><br />I could go on, but I suspect I'm the only one who would be interested.<br /><br />Other that all that crap, though, there are other really well-written pieces sprinkled throughout the novel. At one point Ahern describes staring into a mirror, how your face looks like a stranger's. (I never knew other people did that.) The grieving that Joyce does for her baby, including her wanting to just be alone and feel self-pity - that was great. (Not for Joyce, but you know what I mean.) And the way Joyce and her dad talk about slowing down and enjoying the present rang very true for me. <br /><br />So, in summary, eh. It wasn't my favorite, and I wouldn't recommend it to most people I know - though I do know a few that would probably really like it. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6953296951437209784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_136658148" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136658148" />
    <a title="Oria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3735209-oria"><img alt="Oria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483109706p2/3735209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136658148?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oria" href="/user/show/3735209-oria">Oria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136658148" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10917141076150953905">If anybody asked me what three things I'd like to take with me on an island, I would say 2 books and a sunscreen lotion. I had two books with me on my trip to Koh Chang (Elephant Island), and one of them was Thanks for the Memories. <br/><br/>The reason I bought this book was P.S. I Love You, the movie. I just loved that movie (I must confess Gerard Butler helped a lot in that regard) and even though I haven’t read the book this movie was based on or any other book by this author for that matter, I decide</span>
  <span id="freeText10917141076150953905" style="display:none">If anybody asked me what three things I'd like to take with me on an island, I would say 2 books and a sunscreen lotion. I had two books with me on my trip to Koh Chang (Elephant Island), and one of them was Thanks for the Memories. <br /><br />The reason I bought this book was P.S. I Love You, the movie. I just loved that movie (I must confess Gerard Butler helped a lot in that regard) and even though I haven’t read the book this movie was based on or any other book by this author for that matter, I decided it was time to break the ice. <br /><br />Thanks for the Memories is what I like to refer to as ‘light reading’. After “The Poisonwood Bible” and “The Passage” I felt the need for something different, something romantic and more optimistic.<br />The story is pretty uncomplicated and even though you can see where it’s going, it’s the journey that counts and not the destination, as the saying goes.<br /><br />Joyce and Justin (it almost sounds like Jack and Jill, doesn’t it) are two people at a crossroads in their lives and it almost felt like fate said, let’s take these two and put them together, they would do just fine. How that happens is a bit out of the ordinary and without giving too much away I can safely say it was quite fun to read as Joyce decided to follow her instincts and walk the path that would eventually take her to Justin. <br />Even though the book doesn’t start on a lighter note, there are quite a few scenes and characters too, that soon change that. Joyce’s father spices things up a bit in a very old fashioned and endearing way, followed closely by Justin’s sister in law whose “inch-long leopard print nails and skin-tight leather-trouser-clad hips” brought back to mind Peggy Bundy from the “Married with Children” tv series. <br /><br />All in all an entertaining read, just perfect for a day on the beach under a big tree with the sun winking cheerfully through the leaves above and the sound of the waves in the background.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10917141076150953905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_45350380" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45350380" />
    <a title="Jamieson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/783400-jamieson"><img alt="Jamieson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538046660p2/783400.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45350380?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jamieson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jamieson" href="/user/show/783400-jamieson">Jamieson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45350380" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2983374121228097751">After a horrible accident, Joyce Conway is trying to put her life back together.<br/><br/>Her life and her marriage are in pieces, but Joyce tries to get back to living a normal life, despite advice from others. But something is stopping her. <br/><br/>She keeps having dreams of a beautiful blond haired girl, of places she has never been. She knows things that she shouldn’t about art, about architecture. She sees a beautiful woman in her dreams.<br/><br/>Joyce sees and knows things she should not know. And it all started aft</span>
  <span id="freeText2983374121228097751" style="display:none">After a horrible accident, Joyce Conway is trying to put her life back together.<br /><br />Her life and her marriage are in pieces, but Joyce tries to get back to living a normal life, despite advice from others. But something is stopping her. <br /><br />She keeps having dreams of a beautiful blond haired girl, of places she has never been. She knows things that she shouldn’t about art, about architecture. She sees a beautiful woman in her dreams.<br /><br />Joyce sees and knows things she should not know. And it all started after her accident. Wanting to get to the bottom of things, to discover the reason for her newfound knowledge, Joyce tracks down her blood donor…<br /><br />Justin Hitchcock is a lonely man.<br /><br />He hasn’t dated since his marriage broke up. Instead, he contends himself with touring universities, talking about art, about the only thing he has passion for in life. He knows he’s lonely, knows that he needs to heal.<br /><br />What he doesn’t know is that his life is about to change.<br /><br />When a beautiful woman convinces Justin to give blood for the universities blood drive, Justin has no idea that giving away a few drops of his blood will change his life forever. He has no idea that by giving something from his heart, he may receive the very things he needs to heal it…<br /><br />I have been a long time fan of Cecelia Ahern since her novel P.S. I Love You. I also never miss an episode of her hit show, Samantha Who. Even so, I wondered how good her new novel would be; no one can be so consistently funny, it just doesn’t happened.<br /><br />Well, with Thanks for the Memories, the impossible has indeed happened! This is a heartwarming, laugh out loud romantic comedy that has everything you could want: laughs, strong characters, excellent writing, wonderful plot twists and a happy ending.<br /><br />Though the novel requires you to suspend your disbelief for a moment or two, that’s okay because the characters make this story worth it. Joyce’s father, Justin and Justin’s friends are stand out secondary characters made all the more enjoyable because of Justin and Joyce themselves.<br /><br />They’re such wonderful characters; you’re rooting for them to get together from the very beginning of the novel. It’s rate that I read a novel with such a wonderful cast of characters, but Ahern has created wonderful people that I actually cared about by the time the book was over.<br /><br />Thanks for the memories is a magical, incredible read that will hook you from the first page and not let go. It’s summer reading at it’s best and an absolute delight. If you read one good book this summer, make sure it’s this one.<br /><br />You’ll remember it for a long time to come.<br /><br /> <br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2983374121228097751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer29799908108242740">This is a “will they, won’t they” story with a magical twist. After an accident Joyce finds she “knows” things that she had no knowledge of before – she has acquired an expert knowledge of the arts and architecture. She now likes ballet and opera. Heck, she is even eating meat again after years of being a vegetarian! Even more strange is the fact that she is “seeing” someone else’s memories.<br/><br/>On one of his regular work visits to Dublin, Justin bumps into Joyce, the girl he comes to know as the “gi</span>
  <span id="freeText29799908108242740" style="display:none">This is a “will they, won’t they” story with a magical twist. After an accident Joyce finds she “knows” things that she had no knowledge of before – she has acquired an expert knowledge of the arts and architecture. She now likes ballet and opera. Heck, she is even eating meat again after years of being a vegetarian! Even more strange is the fact that she is “seeing” someone else’s memories.<br /><br />On one of his regular work visits to Dublin, Justin bumps into Joyce, the girl he comes to know as the “girl in the red coat” and immediately feels a connection to her. He keeps bumping into her and losing her time and time again and the story really has you wondering whether or not they will ever get to meet each other and get to know each other properly.<br /><br />It is a charming, witty and often moving read and on the whole, I really enjoyed the story but, unlike other Cecelia Aherne books, I wasn’t gripped and quite often found myself skimming pages.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText16330889292405461267" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this, and every time I read a Cecelia Ahern book I am reminded why I love her writing so much. <div id="review_2354843189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2354843189" />
    <a title="Samama Reza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23148509-samama-reza"><img alt="Samama Reza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598217080p2/23148509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2354843189?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Samama Reza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Samama Reza" href="/user/show/23148509-samama-reza">Samama Reza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2354843189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5003074128135994442">I wonder where Cecelia Ahern gets all these interesting, creative and magical ideas from. The hint of magic she has in all her contemporary fiction stories is something I always aspire in books.<br/><br/>The leading lady in Thanks for the Memories, after an accident, gets a blood transfusion from a stranger - a stranger who has a lot of knowledge on architecture. And now, Joyce has miraculously been gifted with an amazing amount of knowledge on historical architecture, and an obsession on meat. She can’t </span>
  <span id="freeText5003074128135994442" style="display:none">I wonder where Cecelia Ahern gets all these interesting, creative and magical ideas from. The hint of magic she has in all her contemporary fiction stories is something I always aspire in books.<br /><br />The leading lady in Thanks for the Memories, after an accident, gets a blood transfusion from a stranger - a stranger who has a lot of knowledge on architecture. And now, Joyce has miraculously been gifted with an amazing amount of knowledge on historical architecture, and an obsession on meat. She can’t figure out where all this coming from in her head, and at a point she doesn’t even care as she gets drawn to a stranger called Justin – the stranger who had anonymously donated his blood to her.<br /><br />Oh my! *Squeaking*. The plotline might sound kind of dumb and funny, but trust me; the author puts everything in such an interesting and sophisticated way, that you’re going to end up loving the story. And the book had something I absolutely love and admire in all books regardless of how some individuals devotedly hated it. And that is: SLOW BURN ROMANCE. The book was filled with many beautiful quotes and explanations, some even worked therapeutically for me.<br /><br />Joyce had a sweet and soft personality, but that didn’t mean she’d let people step over her. That’s something I found absolutely admirable about her. Justin was funny, handsome and interesting. But oh boy was he an arrogant soul. But as the story progressed, he grew wiser and thus nicer. I loved that about him.<br /><br />However, the ending felt a little unsatisfying. Even though it was all right, I was still expecting a lot more. Some things felt undone. So, 4.5 out of 5 stars. 🌟🌟🌟🌟</span>
  <a data-text-id="5003074128135994442" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16400847361990439242">3,5/5 stars! It was an easy read and a sweet story, though most of the time it felt like the narration was focused more on the relationship between Joyce and her father than the actual story between the two protagonists, Joyce and Justin. Although the events are kind of surreal and not scientifically proven it's an honorable attempt at pointing out the strong connection that two people, with very little in common, may share for, sometimes, unknown reasons.   <span id="freeText16400847361990439242" style="display:none">3,5/5 stars! It was an easy read and a sweet story, though most of the time it felt like the narration was focused more on the relationship between Joyce and her father than the actual story between the two protagonists, Joyce and Justin. Although the events are kind of surreal and not scientifically proven it's an honorable attempt at pointing out the strong connection that two people, with very little in common, may share for, sometimes, unknown reasons. Cecelia Ahern created this book as if the readers were watching an film, the action, the instant changes among scenes and characters, that kind of brought to my mind films like "Serendipity" and "In your eyes". In the end the story seemed a little rushed to me and left me quite emotionally hanging but on the whole it was a really enjoyble book! Also recommendable for doses of laughter where Joyce's adorable old father is involved! Maybe my favourite character in the book!</span>

<div id="review_310667680" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310667680" />
    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/314565-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546883666p2/314565.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310667680?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/314565-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310667680" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13865420817564358194">This book sucked me right in from the riveting 3 page prologue, powerfully, painfully written. While the premise of the book is pretty out there and far-fetched, it was written so convincingly that I couldn't help but be drawn into the lives of the two main characters and found myself blasting through the book to see how it would end. When the characters' hearts were racing I found my own heart beating faster, too. With each missed connection I groaned and sighed in my mind. Reading this book wa</span>
  <span id="freeText13865420817564358194" style="display:none">This book sucked me right in from the riveting 3 page prologue, powerfully, painfully written. While the premise of the book is pretty out there and far-fetched, it was written so convincingly that I couldn't help but be drawn into the lives of the two main characters and found myself blasting through the book to see how it would end. When the characters' hearts were racing I found my own heart beating faster, too. With each missed connection I groaned and sighed in my mind. Reading this book was quite an emotional ride. On top of the mysterious connection and romance angle of the book, I found the supporting characters to be really enjoyable. I loved Doris and Al, Frankie and Kate, and most especially, of course, Joyce's dad. I loved that the author took the time to really define all the relationships (friendships, marriages, parent/child, sibling) in the book and gave the reader a chance to know characters through those relationships. I found this to be a totally delightful read, touching and humorous, romantic and exciting. <br /><br />It should be noted, for those who are sensitive, that there are a handful or so of "F Bombs" in this one. Sigh.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13865420817564358194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Jackie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1147841-jackie"><img alt="Jackie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1240450765p2/1147841.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36644928?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jackie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jackie" href="/user/show/1147841-jackie">Jackie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36644928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10672114711420085197">This will be out in April 2009<br/><br/>Ahern, queen of the "soul mates will find each other" chic lit fairy tales, has another winner on her hands. There's always a bit of magic involved in her tales, but this one has the biggest dose yet. Protagonist Joyce takes a tumble down some stairs, losing her baby (and ultimately her marriage) and needing a blood transfusion. While still in the hospital, she discovers she has all sorts of new knowledge--architectural, artistic, historic, a grasp of languages--tha</span>
  <span id="freeText10672114711420085197" style="display:none">This will be out in April 2009<br /><br />Ahern, queen of the "soul mates will find each other" chic lit fairy tales, has another winner on her hands. There's always a bit of magic involved in her tales, but this one has the biggest dose yet. Protagonist Joyce takes a tumble down some stairs, losing her baby (and ultimately her marriage) and needing a blood transfusion. While still in the hospital, she discovers she has all sorts of new knowledge--architectural, artistic, historic, a grasp of languages--that she had no actual way of having gained. And then the memory flashes begin--of a woman on a picnic blanket, a tow headed little girl she's never met, and a life she has never lived. She's getting intimate glimpses of someone else's past, and she becomes obsessed with figuring out whose. A couple of chance meetings with a tall man set sparks flying and the comedic dance of trying to get two strangers who are meant to be together ACTUALLY together begins. It's a fun, light read coming out just in time for Spring Break. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10672114711420085197" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_360486478" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/360486478" />
    <a title="Inge" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6278820-inge"><img alt="Inge" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556214992p2/6278820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/360486478?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Inge" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Inge" href="/user/show/6278820-inge">Inge</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=feelgood-wholesome">feelgood-wholesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=chicklit">chicklit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6278820-inge?shelf=wishlist-paperback">wishlist-paperback</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer360486478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17778620871311215776"><i>Thanks For the Memories</i> is possibly one of the cutest books I have ever read. It is a typical work by Cecelia Ahern – a cute story laced with just a hint of magic. Absolutely unrealistic, but I don’t think anyone cares. You just enjoy the ride for as long as it lasts.<br/><br/>Justin Hitchcock is a divorced father and an Architecture teacher. He donates blood in order to sleep with the doctor and is a bit of a douche. His life turns completely upside-down when he keeps encountering a certain woman who he </span>
  <span id="freeText17778620871311215776" style="display:none"><i>Thanks For the Memories</i> is possibly one of the cutest books I have ever read. It is a typical work by Cecelia Ahern – a cute story laced with just a hint of magic. Absolutely unrealistic, but I don’t think anyone cares. You just enjoy the ride for as long as it lasts.<br /><br />Justin Hitchcock is a divorced father and an Architecture teacher. He donates blood in order to sleep with the doctor and is a bit of a douche. His life turns completely upside-down when he keeps encountering a certain woman who he feels a connection to. Meet Joyce Conway. She just lost her baby, her fiancé and a job. After a terrible accident, she needs a blood transfusion. After that, things will never be the same again. She feels completely different. Suddenly she appreciates classical music, she likes exquisite kinds of food, the ones she’s never eaten before, and she could tell you all about Architecture. When she meets Justin at a hair salon, it’s all kinds of weird. Just as they try to figure out what the hell is going on, their lives start intertwining and they get more and more fascinated with each other.<br /><br />This is an amazing book. At one moment it lifts your heart and the next page it completely crushes it. It’s an emotional rollercoaster, but you can’t help but love the story. It’s a little slow-paced, but I didn’t mind – I enjoyed every single word. It made me smile, it made me laugh, and it brought tears to my eyes. It’s the little things in the story that make it so good, so wonderful. The characters felt very real to me. Case and point: Joyce’s father. He’s getting older and is going through the first stages of dementia; he calls Joyce Gracie (the name of his late wife); his one leg is longer than the other and despite his special shoes, he still seesaws whenever he walks, up and down, down and up; how he’s so stubborn like a typical old man (we all know an old man like that); how he loves his daughter unconditionally. It’s little habits like those that make a character realistic, and despite his many flaws, I think he was my favourite character.<br /><br />This book may not be for everyone, but it was just what I needed in a time when I felt miserable: a touch of magic and many, many moments to put a smile on my face.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17778620871311215776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_65613264" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/65613264" />
    <a title="Hafsa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1228304-hafsa"><img alt="Hafsa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1218082546p2/1228304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/65613264?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hafsa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hafsa" href="/user/show/1228304-hafsa">Hafsa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone really</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer65613264" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3883506572265654076">This is my first book by Cecelia Ahern, the author of P.S. I Love You (which she wrote when she was 21!) and co-creator of the ABC show "Samantha Who?" <br/><br/>This book was such a good book to read, it took me by surprise because I wasn't expecting to like it as much as I do. The story is well-paced, and has the elements of a thriller/suspense novel, in the sense that it is a page-turner and always leaves you asking, what happens next?<br/><br/>The real gem of the story is Ahern's prose. I was blown away at her </span>
  <span id="freeText3883506572265654076" style="display:none">This is my first book by Cecelia Ahern, the author of P.S. I Love You (which she wrote when she was 21!) and co-creator of the ABC show "Samantha Who?" <br /><br />This book was such a good book to read, it took me by surprise because I wasn't expecting to like it as much as I do. The story is well-paced, and has the elements of a thriller/suspense novel, in the sense that it is a page-turner and always leaves you asking, what happens next?<br /><br />The real gem of the story is Ahern's prose. I was blown away at her acute attention to human behavior and emotions. Whether through the words of her characters, or through the many metaphors in the book, I kept thinking to myself, wow, she knows how to write real, full-fleshed, characters! Another thing I really enjoyed were the thoughtful and poignant moments scattered throughout the book. It made me want to break out a pen and paper just to jot down the quote, or paragraph, because it was so well written and so profound. <br /><br />In terms of technical details, I love her character development. The whole story spans a few months, tops, but her characters(or the way you feel about them, see them),evolve. I remember in the beginning thinking I didn't want to read about a woman going through a very difficult time, made more difficult by her distant relationship with her elderly father. But as the characters evolve, their relationship evolves, and in the end, you can't help but fall in love with their relationship. <br /><br />The one negative thing I will say is that I think the last few pages fizzled a bit for me. It wasn't bad, and maybe that ending is actually the best case scenario considering the story, but I couldn't help feeling "what if" there was more, we could read more about them post everything they've been through? <br /><br />Either way, this is one of my new favorite books: I loved Ahern's voice and her brutally honest portrayal of human emotions, behaviors, and thoughts (the way she wrote about the protagonist's ordeal, you would think she was writing from personal experience!), and I loved the pace and suspense of the book. I highly recommend it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3883506572265654076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sEXVP0HGxZBwDJbuALUpdvOhQTxPQWmAhQypKnptklXWuP5WJ8iNcsxbo80r3P9skX1kFxImm/C2eWCeYiUs/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('V55QaTCDiY+40dmupZtnmoH+vFWTjxqO0OCW6ZArC5UxY3sAVo3BbQSG7I2O8rGA4yKZfs7o6P7jlV9diGO1PA==')})
  }

She is now published in nearly fifty countries, and has sold over twenty-five million copies of her novels worldwide. Two of her books have been adapted as films and she has created several TV series.</span>
